<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Photography</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"><div class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint" id="mw-fr-revisiontag"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><span class="flaggedrevs-icon oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-articleSearch oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-iconWidget" title="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page."></span><span class="fr-toggle-arrow oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicator-down oo-ui-indicatorElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-indicatorWidget" id="mw-fr-revisiontoggle" title="show/hide details"></span></div>
<div id="mw-fr-revisiondetails-wrapper" style="position:relative;"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_details" id="mw-fr-revisiondetails" style="display:none">This is the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pending_changes" title="Wikipedia:Pending changes">latest accepted revision</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:Log&amp;type=review&amp;page=Photography">reviewed</a> on <i>10 October 2022</i>.</div>

<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Creating images by recording light</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Photographic" redirects here. For the image obtained, see <a href="/wiki/Photograph" title="Photograph">Photograph</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Photography_(disambiguation)" title="Photography (disambiguation)">Photography (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox"><caption class="infobox-title">Photography</caption><tbody><tr><td class="infobox-image" colspan="2" style="border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;padding-top:0.4em;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Large_format_camera_lens.jpg"><img alt="Large format camera lens.jpg" data-file-height="271" data-file-width="218" decoding="async" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/Large_format_camera_lens.jpg" width="250"/></a><div class="infobox-caption" style="padding:0.35em 0.35em 0.25em;line-height:1.25em;">Lens and mounting of a large-format camera</div></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Other names</th><td class="infobox-data" class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">Recording light or other electromagnetic radiation</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Inventor</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Louis_Daguerre" title="Louis Daguerre">Louis Daguerre</a> (1839) <br/> <a href="/wiki/Henry_Fox_Talbot" title="Henry Fox Talbot">Henry Fox Talbot</a> (1839)</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Related</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">Stereoscopic, Full-spectrum, Light field, Electrophotography, Photograms, Scanner</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Photography</b> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visual_art" title="Visual art">art</a>, application, and practice of creating durable <a href="/wiki/Image" title="Image">images</a> by recording <a href="/wiki/Light" title="Light">light</a>, either electronically by means of an <a href="/wiki/Image_sensor" title="Image sensor">image sensor</a>, or chemically by means of a light-sensitive material such as <a href="/wiki/Photographic_film" title="Photographic film">photographic film</a>. It is employed in many fields of science, manufacturing (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Photolithography" title="Photolithography">photolithography</a>), and business, as well as its more direct uses for art, <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">film</a> and <a href="/wiki/Video_production" title="Video production">video production</a>, recreational purposes, hobby, and <a href="/wiki/Mass_communication" title="Mass communication">mass communication.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Typically, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lens_(optics)" title="Lens (optics)">lens</a> is used to <a href="/wiki/Focus_(optics)" title="Focus (optics)">focus</a> the light reflected or emitted from objects into a real image on the light-sensitive surface inside a <a href="/wiki/Camera" title="Camera">camera</a> during a timed <a href="/wiki/Exposure_(photography)" title="Exposure (photography)">exposure</a>. With an electronic image sensor, this produces an <a href="/wiki/Charge-coupled_device" title="Charge-coupled device">electrical charge</a> at each <a href="/wiki/Pixel" title="Pixel">pixel</a>, which is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Image_processing" title="Image processing">electronically processed</a> and stored in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Image_file_formats" title="Image file formats">digital image file</a> for subsequent display or processing. The result with <a href="/wiki/Photographic_emulsion" title="Photographic emulsion">photographic emulsion</a> is an invisible <a href="/wiki/Latent_image" title="Latent image">latent image</a>, which is later chemically <a href="/wiki/Photographic_developer" title="Photographic developer">"developed"</a> into a visible image, either <a href="/wiki/Negative_(photography)" title="Negative (photography)">negative</a> or <a href="/wiki/Positive_(photography)" title="Positive (photography)">positive</a>, depending on the purpose of the photographic material and the method of <a href="/wiki/Photographic_processing" title="Photographic processing">processing</a>. A negative image on film is traditionally used to photographically create a positive image on a paper base, known as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photographic_print" title="Photographic print">print</a>, either by using an <a href="/wiki/Enlarger" title="Enlarger">enlarger</a> or by <a href="/wiki/Contact_print" title="Contact print">contact printing</a>.
</p>
